        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Presidentes_del_Per%C3%BA_y_Bolivia_inauguran_Encuentro_Presidencial_y_III_Gabinete_Binacional_Per%C3%BA-Bolivia_(36962597345)_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Former President, <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_presidential_election,_2005" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolivian presidential election, 2005">2005 presidential election</a> with 53.7% of the votes in Bolivian elections.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> On 1 May 2006, Morales announced his intent to <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_gas_conflict" title="Bolivian gas conflict">re-nationalize Bolivian hydrocarbon assets</a> following protests which demanded this action.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> Fulfilling a campaign promise, on 6 August 2006, Morales opened the <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_Constituent_Assembly" title="Bolivian Constituent Assembly">Bolivian Constituent Assembly</a> to begin writing a new constitution aimed at giving more power to the indigenous majority.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In August 2007, a conflict which came to be known as The Calancha Case arose in <a href="/wiki/Sucre" title="Sucre">Sucre</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view#Due_and_undue_weight" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view"><span title="The material near this tag may be giving undue weight to a viewpoint or idea. (September 2020)">undue weight?</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:Bolivia#undue" title="Talk:Bolivia">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> Local citizens demanded that an official discussion of the seat of government be included in the agenda of the full body of the Bolivian Constituent Assembly. The people of Sucre wanted to make Sucre the full capital of the country, including returning the executive and legislative branches to the city, but the government rejected the demand as impractical. Three people died in the conflict and as many as 500 were wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> The result of the conflict was to include text in the constitution stating that the capital of Bolivia is officially Sucre, while leaving the executive and legislative branches in La Paz. In May 2008, Evo Morales was a signatory to the <a href="/wiki/UNASUR_Constitutive_Treaty" title="UNASUR Constitutive Treaty">UNASUR Constitutive Treaty</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">Union of South American Nations</a>. </p>
      <p>2009 marked the creation of a new constitution and the renaming of the country to the Plurinational State of Bolivia. The previous constitution did not allow a consecutive reelection of a president, but the new constitution allowed just for one reelection, starting the dispute if Evo Morales was enabled to run for a second term arguing he was elected under the last constitution. This also triggered a new general election in which Evo Morales was re-elected with 61.36% of the vote. His party, <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_Socialism_(Bolivia)" title="Movement for Socialism (Bolivia)">Movement for Socialism</a>, also won a two-thirds majority in both houses of the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Bolivia" class="mw-redirect" title="National Congress of Bolivia">National Congress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup> By the year 2013 after being reelected under the new constitution, Evo Morales and his party attempt for a third term as President of Bolivia. The opposition argued that a third term would be unconstitutional but the Bolivian Constitutional Court ruled that Morales' first term under the previous constitution, did not count towards his term limit.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup> This allowed Evo Morales to run for a third term in 2014, and he was re-elected with 64.22% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> On 17 October 2015, Morales surpassed <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_de_Santa_Cruz" title="Andrés de Santa Cruz">Andrés de Santa Cruz</a>'s nine years, eight months, and twenty-four days in office and became Bolivia's longest serving president.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup> During his third term, Evo Morales began to plan for a fourth, and the <a href="/wiki/2016_Bolivian_constitutional_referendum" title="2016 Bolivian constitutional referendum">2016 Bolivian constitutional referendum</a> asked voters to override the constitution and allow Evo Morales to run for an additional term in office. Morales narrowly lost the referendum,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> however in 2017 his party then petitioned the Bolivian Constitutional Court to override the constitution on the basis that the <a href="/wiki/American_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="American Convention on Human Rights">American Convention on Human Rights</a> made term limits a human rights violation.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_Court_of_Human_Rights" title="Inter-American Court of Human Rights">Inter-American Court of Human Rights</a> determined that term limits are not a human rights violation in 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup> however, once again the Bolivian Constitutional Court ruled that Morales has the permission to run for a fourth term in the 2019 elections, and the permission was not retracted. "[...] the country’s highest court overruled the constitution, scrapping term limits altogether for every office. Morales can now run for a fourth term in 2019 – and for every election thereafter." described an article in The Guardian in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Interim_government_2019.E2.80.932020"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Interim_government_2019–2020">Interim government 2019–2020</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Interim government 2019–2020">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/2019_Bolivian_general_election" title="2019 Bolivian general election">2019 Bolivian general election</a> and <a href="/wiki/2019_Bolivian_political_crisis" title="2019 Bolivian political crisis">2019 Bolivian political crisis</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-POV plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-POV" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <img alt="Unbalanced scales.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/45px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png" decoding="async" width="45" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/68px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/90px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="354">
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           The <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">neutrality</a> of this article is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NPOV_dispute" title="Wikipedia:NPOV dispute">disputed</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Bolivia##" title="Talk:Bolivia">talk page</a>. Please do not remove this message until <a href="/wiki/Template:POV#When_to_remove" title="Template:POV">conditions to do so are met</a>.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2020</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>During the 2019 elections, the transmission of the unofficial quick counting process was interrupted; at the time, Morales had a lead of 46.86 percent to Mesa's 36.72, after 95.63 percent of tally sheets were counted.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2019_Bolivian_general_election" title="2019 Bolivian general election"><i>Transmisión de Resultados Electorales Preliminares</i> (TREP)</a> is a quick count process used in Latin America as a transparency measure in electoral processes that is meant to provide a preliminary results on election day, and its shutdown without further explanation<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> raised consternation among opposition politicians and certain election monitors.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> Two days after the interruption, the official count showed Morales fractionally clearing the 10-point margin he needed to avoid a runoff election, with the final official tally counted as 47.08 percent to Mesa's 36.51 percent, starting a wave of protests and tension in the country. </p>
      <p>Amidst allegations of fraud perpetrated by the Morales government, widespread <a href="/wiki/2019_Bolivian_protests" title="2019 Bolivian protests">protests</a> organized to dispute the election. On 10 November, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a> (OAS) released a preliminary report concluding several irregularities in the election,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> though these findings were heavily disputed.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> The Center for Economic and Policy Research (CEPR) concluded that "it is very likely that Morales won the required 10 percentage point margin to win in the first round of the election on 20 October 2019."<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> David Rosnick, an economist for CEPR, showed that "a basic coding error" was discovered in the OAS's data, which explained that the OAS had misused its own data when it ordered the time stamps on the tally sheets alphabetically rather than chronologically.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> However, the OAS stood by its findings arguing that the "researchers’ work did not address many of the allegations mentioned in the OAS report, including the accusation that Bolivian officials maintained hidden servers that could have permitted the alteration of results".<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> Additionally, observers from the European Union released a report with similar findings and conclusions as the OAS.<sup id="cite_ref-eu12_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eu12-70">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> The tech security company hired by the TSE (under the Morales administration) to audit the elections, also stated that there were multiple irregularities and violations of procedure and that "our function as an auditor security company is to declare everything that was found, and much of what was found supports the conclusion that the electoral process should be declared null and void".<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> The New York Times reported on 7 June 2020, that the OAS analysis immediately after the 20 October election was flawed yet fuelled "a chain of events that changed the South American nation’s history".<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After weeks of protests, Morales resigned on national television shortly after the Commander-in-Chief of the armed forces General <a href="/wiki/Williams_Kaliman" title="Williams Kaliman">Williams Kaliman</a> had urged that he do so in order to restore "peace and stability".<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup> Morales flew to Mexico and was granted asylum there, along with his vice president and several other members of his government.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> Opposition Senator <a href="/wiki/Jeanine_%C3%81%C3%B1ez" title="Jeanine Áñez">Jeanine Áñez</a>'s declared herself interim president, claiming constitutional succession after the president, vice president and bot head of the legislature chambers. She was confirmed as interim president by the constitutional court who declared her succession to be constitutional and automatic.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> Morales, his supporters, the Governments of Mexico and Nicaragua, and other personalities argue the event as a coup d'état. However, local investigators and analysts pointed out that even after Morales' resignation and during all of Añez's term in office, the Chamber of Senators and Deputies were ruled by Morales' political party MAS, making it impossible to be a coup d'état as such an event would not allow the original government to maintain legislative power.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup> International politicians, scholars and journalists are divided between describing the event as a coup or a spontaneous social uprising against an unconstitutional fourth-term.<sup id="cite_ref-BC2_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BC2-84">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> Protests to reinstate Morales as president continued becoming highly violent: burning public buses and private houses, destroying public infrastructure and pedestrians.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> The protests were met with more violence by security forces against Morales supporters after Áñez exempted police and military from criminal responsibility in operations for "the restoration of order and public stability".<sup id="cite_ref-Estes_20192_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Estes_20192-96">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In April 2020, the interim government took out a loan of more that $327 million from the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> in order to meet the country's needs during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sopitas1802212_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sopitas1802212-98">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>New elections were scheduled for 3 May 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> In response to the Coronavirus pandemic, the Bolivian electoral body, the TSE, made an announcement postponing the election. MAS reluctantly agreed with the first delay only. A date for the new election was delayed twice more, in the face of massive protests and violence.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> The final proposed date for the elections was 18 October 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup> Observers from the OAS, UNIORE, and the UN all reported that they did not find any fraudulent actions in the 2020 elections.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/2020_Bolivian_general_election" title="2020 Bolivian general election">general election</a> had a record voter turnout of 88.4% and ended in a landslide win for MAS which took 55.1% of the votes compared to 28.8% for centrist former president Carlos Mesa. Both Mesa and Áñez conceded defeat. "I congratulate the winners and I ask them to govern thinking in Bolivia and in our democracy," Áñez said on Twitter.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_of_Luis_Arce:_2020_-">Government of Luis Arce: 2020 -</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Government of Luis Arce: 2020 -">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In February 2021, the Arce government returned an amount of around $351 million to the IMF. This comprised a loan of $327 million taken out by the interim government in April 2020 and interest of around $24 million. The government said it returned to loan to protect Bolivia's economic sovereignty and because the conditions attached to the loan were unacceptable.<sup id="cite_ref-sopitas1802212_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sopitas1802212-98">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Bolivia" title="Geography of Bolivia">Geography of Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_image_of_Bolivia_in_June_2002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Satellite_image_of_Bolivia_in_June_2002.jpg/220px-Satellite_image_of_Bolivia_in_June_2002.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Satellite_image_of_Bolivia_in_June_2002.jpg/330px-Satellite_image_of_Bolivia_in_June_2002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Satellite_image_of_Bolivia_in_June_2002.jpg/440px-Satellite_image_of_Bolivia_in_June_2002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5279" data-file-height="6079"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Satellite_image_of_Bolivia_in_June_2002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Satellite image of Bolivia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Altiplano.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Altiplano.jpg/220px-Altiplano.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Altiplano.jpg/330px-Altiplano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Altiplano.jpg/440px-Altiplano.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Altiplano.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bolivian Altiplano.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sol_de_Ma%C3%B1ana_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Sol_de_Ma%C3%B1ana_2018.jpg/220px-Sol_de_Ma%C3%B1ana_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Sol_de_Ma%C3%B1ana_2018.jpg/330px-Sol_de_Ma%C3%B1ana_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Sol_de_Ma%C3%B1ana_2018.jpg/440px-Sol_de_Ma%C3%B1ana_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sol_de_Ma%C3%B1ana_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sol de Mañana (<i>Morning Sun</i> in Spanish), a geothermal field in <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Avaroa_Andean_Fauna_National_Reserve" title="Eduardo Avaroa Andean Fauna National Reserve">Eduardo Avaroa Andean Fauna National Reserve</a>, Potosi Department, southwestern Bolivia. The area, characterized by intense volcanic activity, with sulphur spring fields and mud lakes, has indeed no geysers but rather holes that emit pressurized steam up to 50 metres high.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bolivia is located in the <a href="/wiki/Central_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Central zone">central zone</a> of <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, between 57°26'–69°38'W and 9°38'–22°53'S. With an area of 1,098,581 square kilometres (424,164&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), Bolivia is the world's 28th-largest country, and the fifth largest country in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup> extending from the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Central Andes</a> through part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Pantanal" title="Pantanal">Pantanal</a> and as far as the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon</a>. The geographic center of the country is the so-called <i>Puerto Estrella</i> ("Star Port") on the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_(Bolivia)" title="Río Grande (Bolivia)">Río Grande</a>, in <a href="/wiki/%C3%91uflo_de_Ch%C3%A1vez_Province" title="Ñuflo de Chávez Province">Ñuflo de Chávez Province</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Department,_Bolivia" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Cruz Department, Bolivia">Santa Cruz Department</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">geography</a> of the country exhibits a great variety of terrain and climates. Bolivia has a high level of <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> considered one of the greatest in the world, as well as several <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregions</a> with ecological sub-units such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">Altiplano</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">tropical rainforests</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a>), dry <a href="/wiki/Valley" title="Valley">valleys</a>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Chiquitania" title="Chiquitania">Chiquitania</a></i>, which is a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_grasslands,_savannas,_and_shrublands" title="Tropical and subtropical grasslands, savannas, and shrublands">tropical savanna</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="First claim about biodiversity is substaintiated, but the rest of the sentence's source is unclear. (February 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> These areas feature enormous variations in altitude, from an elevation of 6,542 metres (21,463&nbsp;ft) above sea level in <a href="/wiki/Nevado_Sajama" title="Nevado Sajama">Nevado Sajama</a> to nearly 70 metres (230&nbsp;ft) along the <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_River" title="Paraguay River">Paraguay River</a>. Although a country of great geographic diversity, Bolivia has remained a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> since the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a>. <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Su%C3%A1rez" title="Puerto Suárez">Puerto Suárez</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Mat%C3%ADas,_Santa_Cruz" title="San Matías, Santa Cruz">San Matías</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Quijarro" title="Puerto Quijarro">Puerto Quijarro</a> are located in the <a href="/wiki/Pantanal" title="Pantanal">Bolivian Pantanal</a>. </p>
      <p>Bolivia can be divided into three <a href="/wiki/Physical_geography" title="Physical geography">physiographic</a> regions: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><b>The Andean region</b> in the southwest spans 28% of the national territory, extending over 307,603 square kilometres (118,766&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). This area is located above 3,000 metres (9,800&nbsp;ft) altitude and is located between two big Andean chains, the <i><a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Occidental_(Bolivia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cordillera Occidental (Bolivia)">Cordillera Occidental</a></i> ("Western Range") and the <i><a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Bolivia)" title="Cordillera Central (Bolivia)">Cordillera Central</a></i> ("Central Range"), with some of the highest spots in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Nevado_Sajama" title="Nevado Sajama">Nevado Sajama</a>, with an altitude of 6,542 metres (21,463&nbsp;ft), and the <a href="/wiki/Illimani" title="Illimani">Illimani</a>, at 6,462 metres (21,201&nbsp;ft). Also located in the Cordillera Central is <a href="/wiki/Lake_Titicaca" title="Lake Titicaca">Lake Titicaca</a>, the highest commercially navigable lake in the world and the largest lake in South America;<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> the lake is shared with <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>. Also in this region are the <i><a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">Altiplano</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Salar_de_Uyuni" title="Salar de Uyuni">Salar de Uyuni</a></i>, which is the largest <a href="/wiki/Salt_pan_(geology)" title="Salt pan (geology)">salt flat</a> in the world and an important source of <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">lithium</a>.</li> 
       <li>The <b>Sub-Andean region</b> in the center and south of the country is an intermediate region between the <i><a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">Altiplano</a></i> and the eastern <i><a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">llanos</a></i> (plain); this region comprises 13% of the territory of Bolivia, extending over 142,815&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (55,141&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), and encompassing the Bolivian valleys and the Yungas region. It is distinguished by its farming activities and its temperate climate.</li> 
       <li>The <b>Llanos region</b> in the northeast comprises 59% of the territory, with 648,163&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (250,257&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). It is located to the north of the Cordillera Central and extends from the Andean foothills to the <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_River" title="Paraguay River">Paraguay River</a>. It is a region of flat land and small plateaus, all covered by extensive rain forests containing enormous biodiversity. The region is below 400 metres (1,300&nbsp;ft) above sea level.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Bolivia has three <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">drainage basins</a>: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>The first is the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon Basin</a>, also called the North Basin (724,000&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (280,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)/66% of the territory). The rivers of this basin generally have big <a href="/wiki/Meander" title="Meander">meanders</a> which form lakes such as <a href="/wiki/Murillo_Lake" title="Murillo Lake">Murillo Lake</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pando_Department" title="Pando Department">Pando Department</a>. The main Bolivian <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">tributary</a> to the Amazon basin is the <a href="/wiki/Mamor%C3%A9_River" title="Mamoré River">Mamoré River</a>, with a length of 2,000&nbsp;km (1,200&nbsp;mi) running north to the confluence with the <a href="/wiki/Beni_River" title="Beni River">Beni River</a>, 1,113&nbsp;km (692&nbsp;mi) in length and the second most important river of the country. The Beni River, along with the <a href="/wiki/Madeira_River" title="Madeira River">Madeira River</a>, forms the main tributary of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon River</a>. From east to west, the basin is formed by other important rivers, such as the <a href="/wiki/Madre_de_Dios_River" title="Madre de Dios River">Madre de Dios River</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Orthon_River" title="Orthon River">Orthon River</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Abuna_River" title="Abuna River">Abuna River</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Yata_River" title="Yata River">Yata River</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Guapor%C3%A9_River" title="Guaporé River">Guaporé River</a>. The most important lakes are <a href="/wiki/Rogaguado_Lake" title="Rogaguado Lake">Rogaguado Lake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rogagua_Lake" title="Rogagua Lake">Rogagua Lake</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jara_Lake" title="Jara Lake">Jara Lake</a>.</li> 
       <li>The second is the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_Basin" title="Río de la Plata Basin">Río de la Plata Basin</a>, also called the South Basin (229,500&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (88,600&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)/21% of the territory). The tributaries in this basin are in general less abundant than the ones forming the Amazon Basin. The Rio de la Plata Basin is mainly formed by the <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_River" title="Paraguay River">Paraguay River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pilcomayo_River" title="Pilcomayo River">Pilcomayo River</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bermejo_River" title="Bermejo River">Bermejo River</a>. The most important lakes are <a href="/wiki/Uberaba_Lake" title="Uberaba Lake">Uberaba Lake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mandior%C3%A9_Lake" title="Mandioré Lake">Mandioré Lake</a>, both located in the Bolivian marshland.</li> 
       <li>The third basin is the <b>Central Basin</b>, which is an <a href="/wiki/Endorheic_basin" title="Endorheic basin">endorheic basin</a> (145,081 square kilometres (56,016&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)/13% of the territory). The <i><a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">Altiplano</a></i> has large numbers of lakes and rivers that do not run into any ocean because they are enclosed by the Andean mountains. The most important river is the <a href="/wiki/Desaguadero_River_(Bolivia)" title="Desaguadero River (Bolivia)">Desaguadero River</a>, with a length of 436&nbsp;km (271&nbsp;mi), the longest river of the <i>Altiplano</i>; it begins in <a href="/wiki/Lake_Titicaca" title="Lake Titicaca">Lake Titicaca</a> and then runs in a southeast direction to <a href="/wiki/Poop%C3%B3_Lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Poopó Lake">Poopó Lake</a>. The basin is then formed by Lake Titicaca, Lake Poopó, the Desaguadero River, and great salt flats, including the <i><a href="/wiki/Salar_de_Uyuni" title="Salar de Uyuni">Salar de Uyuni</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Coipasa_Lake" title="Coipasa Lake">Coipasa Lake</a>.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bolivia_prec.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Bolivia_prec.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Bolivia_prec.tif.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Bolivia_prec.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Bolivia_prec.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Bolivia_prec.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Bolivia_prec.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="878" data-file-height="662"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bolivia_prec.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mean annual precipitation in Bolivia<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_BOL_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Koppen-Geiger_Map_BOL_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_BOL_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Koppen-Geiger_Map_BOL_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_BOL_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Koppen-Geiger_Map_BOL_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_BOL_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1328" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_BOL_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bolivia map of Köppen climate classification.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Bolivia" title="Geology of Bolivia">geology of Bolivia</a> comprises a variety of different <a href="/wiki/Lithology" title="Lithology">lithologies</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">tectonic</a> and sedimentary environments. On a synoptic scale, geological units coincide with topographical units. Most elementally, the country is divided into a mountainous western area affected by the <a href="/wiki/Subduction" title="Subduction">subduction</a> processes in the Pacific and an eastern lowlands of stable <a href="/wiki/Platform_(geology)" title="Platform (geology)">platforms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shield_(geology)" title="Shield (geology)">shields</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pista_de_esqu%C3%AD_de_Chacaltaya_Bolivia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Pista_de_esqu%C3%AD_de_Chacaltaya_Bolivia.jpg/220px-Pista_de_esqu%C3%AD_de_Chacaltaya_Bolivia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="366" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Pista_de_esqu%C3%AD_de_Chacaltaya_Bolivia.jpg/330px-Pista_de_esqu%C3%AD_de_Chacaltaya_Bolivia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Pista_de_esqu%C3%AD_de_Chacaltaya_Bolivia.jpg/440px-Pista_de_esqu%C3%AD_de_Chacaltaya_Bolivia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1610" data-file-height="2675"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pista_de_esqu%C3%AD_de_Chacaltaya_Bolivia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Chacaltaya" title="Chacaltaya">Chacaltaya</a> Ski Resort, <a href="/wiki/La_Paz_Department_(Bolivia)" title="La Paz Department (Bolivia)">La Paz Department</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The climate of Bolivia varies drastically from one eco-region to the other, from the tropics in the eastern <i><a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">llanos</a></i> to a <a href="/wiki/Polar_climate" title="Polar climate">polar climate</a> in the western Andes. The summers are warm, humid in the east and dry in the west, with rains that often modify temperatures, humidity, winds, <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">atmospheric pressure</a> and evaporation, yielding very different climates in different areas. When the climatological phenomenon known as <i><a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o-Southern_Oscillation" class="mw-redirect" title="El Niño-Southern Oscillation">El Niño</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> takes place, it causes great alterations in the weather. Winters are very cold in the west, and it snows in the mountain ranges, while in the western regions, windy days are more common. The autumn is dry in the non-tropical regions. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><i>Llanos</i>. A <a href="/wiki/Humidity" title="Humidity">humid</a> <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a> with an average temperature of 25&nbsp;°C (77&nbsp;°F). The wind coming from the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a> causes significant rainfall. In May, there is low precipitation because of dry winds, and most days have clear skies. Even so, winds from the south, called <i>surazos</i>, can bring cooler temperatures lasting several days.</li> 
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">Altiplano</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">Desert</a>-<a href="/wiki/Polar_climate" title="Polar climate">Polar</a> climates, with strong and cold winds. The average temperature ranges from 15 to 20&nbsp;°C. At night, temperatures descend drastically to slightly above 0&nbsp;°C, while during the day, the weather is dry and <a href="/wiki/Sunlight" title="Sunlight">solar radiation</a> is high. <a href="/wiki/Ground_frost" title="Ground frost">Ground frosts</a> occur every month, and snow is frequent.</li> 
       <li>Valleys and <i>Yungas</i>. <a href="/wiki/Temperateness" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperateness">Temperate</a> climate. The humid northeastern winds are pushed to the mountains, making this region very humid and rainy. Temperatures are cooler at higher elevations. Snow occurs at altitudes of 2,000 metres (6,600&nbsp;ft).</li> 
       <li><i><a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Chaco</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">Subtropical</a> <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a>. Rainy and humid in January and the rest of the year, with warm days and cold nights.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Issues_with_climate_change">Issues with climate change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Issues with climate change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Bolivia is especially vulnerable to the negative consequences of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>. Twenty percent of the world's tropical <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">glaciers</a> are located within the country,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> and are more sensitive to change in temperature due to the tropical climate they are located in. Temperatures in the Andes increased by 0.1&nbsp;°C per decade from 1939 to 1998, and more recently the rate of increase has tripled (to 0.33&nbsp;°C per decade from 1980 to 2005),<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> causing glaciers to recede at an accelerated pace and create unforeseen water shortages in Andean agricultural towns. Farmers have taken to temporary city jobs when there is poor yield for their crops, while others have started permanently leaving the agricultural sector and are migrating to nearby towns for other forms of work;<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> some view these migrants as the first generation of <a href="/wiki/Environmental_migrant" title="Environmental migrant">climate refugees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> Cities that neighboring agricultural land, like El Alto, face the challenge of providing services to the influx of new migrants; because there is no alternative water source, the city's water source is now being constricted. </p>
      <p>Bolivia's government and other agencies have acknowledged the need to instill new policies battling the <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change" title="Effects of climate change">effects of climate change</a>. The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> has provided funding through the Climate Investment Funds (CIF) and are using the Pilot Program for Climate Resilience (PPCR II) to construct new <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a> systems, protect riverbanks and basins, and work on building water resources with the help of indigenous communities.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> Bolivia has also implemented the Bolivian Strategy on Climate Change, which is based on taking action in these four areas: </p> 
      <ol>
       <li>Promoting clean development in Bolivia by introducing technological changes in the agriculture, forestry, and industrial sectors, aimed to reduce GHG emissions with a positive impact on development.</li> 
       <li>Contributing to carbon management in forests, wetlands and other managed natural ecosystems.</li> 
       <li>Increasing effectiveness in energy supply and use to mitigate effects of GHG emissions and risk of contingencies.</li> 
       <li>Focus on increased and efficient observations, and understanding of environmental changes in Bolivia to develop effective and timely responses.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup></li>
      </ol> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Bolivia, with an enormous variety of <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">organisms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a>, is part of the "<a href="/wiki/Like-Minded_Megadiverse_Countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Like-Minded Megadiverse Countries">Like-Minded Megadiverse Countries</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bolivia's variable altitudes, ranging from 90–6,542 metres (295–21,463&nbsp;ft) above sea level, allow for a vast biologic diversity. The territory of Bolivia comprises four types of <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">biomes</a>, 32 ecological regions, and 199 ecosystems. Within this geographic area there are several natural parks and reserves such as the <a href="/wiki/Noel_Kempff_Mercado_National_Park" title="Noel Kempff Mercado National Park">Noel Kempff Mercado National Park</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Madidi_National_Park" title="Madidi National Park">Madidi National Park</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tunari_National_Park" title="Tunari National Park">Tunari National Park</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Avaroa_Andean_Fauna_National_Reserve" title="Eduardo Avaroa Andean Fauna National Reserve">Eduardo Avaroa Andean Fauna National Reserve</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Kaa-Iya_del_Gran_Chaco_National_Park_and_Integrated_Management_Natural_Area" title="Kaa-Iya del Gran Chaco National Park and Integrated Management Natural Area">Kaa-Iya del Gran Chaco National Park and Integrated Management Natural Area</a>, among others. </p>
      <p>Bolivia boasts over 17,000 species of seed plants, including over 1,200 species of <a href="/wiki/Fern" title="Fern">fern</a>, 1,500 species of <i><a href="/wiki/Marchantiophyta" title="Marchantiophyta">marchantiophyta</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Moss" title="Moss">moss</a>, and at least 800 species of <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">fungus</a>. In addition, there are more than 3,000 species of <a href="/wiki/Medicinal_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Medicinal plant">medicinal plants</a>. Bolivia is considered the place of origin for such species as <a href="/wiki/Capsicum_pubescens" title="Capsicum pubescens">peppers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Capsicum" title="Capsicum">chili peppers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">peanuts</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Phaseolus_vulgaris" title="Phaseolus vulgaris">common beans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">yucca</a>, and several species of palm. Bolivia also naturally produces over 4,000 kinds of <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a>. The country had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 8.47/10, ranking it 21st globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-121">[119]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bolivia has more than 2,900 animal species, including 398 mammals, over 1,400 birds (about 14% of birds known in the world, being the sixth most diverse country in terms of bird species)<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (February 2014)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup>, 204 <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibians</a>, 277 <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">reptiles</a>, and 635 fish, all <a href="/wiki/Fresh_water" title="Fresh water">fresh water</a> fish as Bolivia is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a>. In addition, there are more than 3,000 types of <a href="/wiki/Lepidoptera" title="Lepidoptera">butterfly</a>, and more than 60 <a href="/wiki/Domestication" title="Domestication">domestic animals</a>. </p>
      <p>In 2020 a new species of snake, the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Fer-De-Lance_Viper" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain Fer-De-Lance Viper">Mountain Fer-De-Lance Viper</a>, was discovered in Bolivia.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bolivia has gained global attention for its '<a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_Rights_of_Mother_Earth" title="Law of the Rights of Mother Earth">Law of the Rights of Mother Earth</a>', which accords nature the same rights as humans.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Bolivia" title="Politics of Bolivia">Politics of Bolivia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Bolivia" title="Foreign relations of Bolivia">Foreign relations of Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_de_la_Asamblea_Legislativa_de_Bolivia,_vista_lateral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Palacio_de_la_Asamblea_Legislativa_de_Bolivia%2C_vista_lateral.jpg/220px-Palacio_de_la_Asamblea_Legislativa_de_Bolivia%2C_vista_lateral.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Palacio_de_la_Asamblea_Legislativa_de_Bolivia%2C_vista_lateral.jpg/330px-Palacio_de_la_Asamblea_Legislativa_de_Bolivia%2C_vista_lateral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Palacio_de_la_Asamblea_Legislativa_de_Bolivia%2C_vista_lateral.jpg/440px-Palacio_de_la_Asamblea_Legislativa_de_Bolivia%2C_vista_lateral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_de_la_Asamblea_Legislativa_de_Bolivia,_vista_lateral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The government building of the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Bolivia" class="mw-redirect" title="National Congress of Bolivia">National Congress of Bolivia</a> in central <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bolivia has been governed by democratically elected governments since 1982; prior to that, it was governed by various dictatorships. Presidents <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Siles_Zuazo" title="Hernán Siles Zuazo">Hernán Siles Zuazo</a> (1982–85) and <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADctor_Paz_Estenssoro" title="Víctor Paz Estenssoro">Víctor Paz Estenssoro</a> (1985–89) began a tradition of ceding power peacefully which has continued, although three presidents have stepped down in the face of extraordinary circumstances: <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_S%C3%A1nchez_de_Lozada" title="Gonzalo Sánchez de Lozada">Gonzalo Sánchez de Lozada</a> in 2003, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Mesa" title="Carlos Mesa">Carlos Mesa</a> in 2005, and <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> in 2019. </p>
      <p>Bolivia's multiparty democracy has seen a wide variety of parties in the presidency and parliament, although the <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Nationalist_Movement" title="Revolutionary Nationalist Movement">Revolutionary Nationalist Movement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Democratic_Action" title="Nationalist Democratic Action">Nationalist Democratic Action</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Left_Movement_(Bolivia)" title="Revolutionary Left Movement (Bolivia)">Revolutionary Left Movement</a> predominated from 1985 to 2005. On 11 November 2019, all senior governmental positions were vacated following <a href="/wiki/2019_Bolivian_political_crisis" title="2019 Bolivian political crisis">the resignation of Evo Morales and his government</a>. On 13 November 2019, <a href="/wiki/Jeanine_%C3%81%C3%B1ez" title="Jeanine Áñez">Jeanine Áñez</a>, a former senator representing Beni, declared herself acting <a href="/wiki/President_of_Bolivia" title="President of Bolivia">President of Bolivia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Luis_Arce" title="Luis Arce">Luis Arce</a> was elected on 23 October 2020; he took office as president on 8 November 2020. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bolivia" title="Constitution of Bolivia">constitution</a>, drafted in 2006–07 and approved in 2009, provides for balanced executive, legislative, judicial, and electoral powers, as well as several levels of autonomy. The traditionally strong executive branch tends to overshadow the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Bolivia" class="mw-redirect" title="National Congress of Bolivia">Congress</a>, whose role is generally limited to debating and approving legislation initiated by the executive. The judiciary, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Bolivia" title="Supreme Court of Bolivia">Supreme Court</a> and departmental and lower courts, has long been riddled with corruption and inefficiency. Through revisions to the constitution in 1994, and subsequent laws, the government has initiated potentially far-reaching reforms in the judicial system as well as increasing decentralizing powers to departments, municipalities, and indigenous territories. </p>
      <p>The executive branch is headed by a president and vice president, and consists of a variable number (currently, 20) of government <a href="/wiki/Ministry_(government_department)" title="Ministry (government department)">ministries</a>. The president is elected to a five-year term by <a href="/wiki/Direct_election" title="Direct election">popular vote</a>, and governs from the Presidential Palace (popularly called the Burnt Palace, <i>Palacio Quemado</i>) in La Paz. In the case that no candidate receives an <a href="/wiki/Absolute_majority" class="mw-redirect" title="Absolute majority">absolute majority</a> of the popular vote or more than 40% of the vote with an advantage of more than 10% over the second-place finisher, a run-off is to be held among the two candidates most voted.<sup id="cite_ref-presidencia.gob.bo_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-presidencia.gob.bo-125">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <i>Asamblea Legislativa Plurinacional</i> (<a href="/wiki/Plurinational_Legislative_Assembly" title="Plurinational Legislative Assembly">Plurinational Legislative Assembly</a> or National Congress) has <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">two chambers</a>. The <i>Cámara de Diputados</i> (<a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_(Bolivia)" title="Chamber of Deputies (Bolivia)">Chamber of Deputies</a>) has 130 members elected to five-year terms, 63 from single-member districts (<i>circunscripciones</i>), 60 by proportional representation, and seven by the minority indigenous peoples of seven departments. The <i>Cámara de Senadores</i> (<a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Senators_(Bolivia)" title="Chamber of Senators (Bolivia)">Chamber of Senators</a>) has 36 members (four per department). Members of the Assembly are elected to five-year terms. The body has its headquarters on the <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Murillo" title="Plaza Murillo">Plaza Murillo</a> in La Paz, but also holds honorary sessions elsewhere in Bolivia. The Vice President serves as titular head of the combined Assembly. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:20170805_Bolivia_1195_crop_Sucre_sRGB_(26204170499).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/20170805_Bolivia_1195_crop_Sucre_sRGB_%2826204170499%29.jpg/220px-20170805_Bolivia_1195_crop_Sucre_sRGB_%2826204170499%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/20170805_Bolivia_1195_crop_Sucre_sRGB_%2826204170499%29.jpg/330px-20170805_Bolivia_1195_crop_Sucre_sRGB_%2826204170499%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/20170805_Bolivia_1195_crop_Sucre_sRGB_%2826204170499%29.jpg/440px-20170805_Bolivia_1195_crop_Sucre_sRGB_%2826204170499%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3417" data-file-height="2563"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:20170805_Bolivia_1195_crop_Sucre_sRGB_(26204170499).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Supreme Court Building in the capital of Bolivia, <a href="/wiki/Sucre" title="Sucre">Sucre</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The judiciary consists of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Justice_(Bolivia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Court of Justice (Bolivia)">Supreme Court of Justice</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Plurinational_Constitutional_Court" title="Plurinational Constitutional Court">Plurinational Constitutional Court</a>, the Judiciary Council, Agrarian and Environmental Court, and District (departmental) and lower courts. In October 2011, Bolivia held its first judicial elections to choose members of the national courts by popular vote, a reform brought about by Evo Morales. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Plurinational_Electoral_Organ" title="Plurinational Electoral Organ">Plurinational Electoral Organ</a> is an independent branch of government which replaced the <a href="/wiki/National_Electoral_Court_of_Bolivia" title="National Electoral Court of Bolivia">National Electoral Court</a> in 2010. The branch consists of the Supreme Electoral Court, the nine Departmental Electoral Court, Electoral Judges, the anonymously selected Juries at Election Tables, and Electoral Notaries.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> Wilfredo Ovando presides over the seven-member Supreme Electoral Court. Its operations are mandated by the Constitution and regulated by the Electoral Regime Law (Law 026, passed 2010). The Organ's first elections were the country's first <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_judicial_election,_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolivian judicial election, 2011">judicial election</a> in October 2011, and five municipal special elections held in 2011. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capital">Capital</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Capital">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Bolivia has its constitutionally recognized capital in <a href="/wiki/Sucre" title="Sucre">Sucre</a>, while <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a> is the seat of government. La Plata (now Sucre) was proclaimed the provisional capital of the newly independent Alto Perú (later, Bolivia) on 1 July 1826.<sup id="cite_ref-DicGeo_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DicGeo-127">[125]</a></sup> On 12 July 1839, President <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_de_Velasco" title="José Miguel de Velasco">José Miguel de Velasco</a> proclaimed a law naming the city as the capital of Bolivia, and renaming it in honor of the revolutionary leader <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Sucre" title="Antonio José de Sucre">Antonio José de Sucre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DicGeo_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DicGeo-127">[125]</a></sup> The Bolivian seat of government moved to La Paz at the start of the twentieth century as a consequence of Sucre's relative remoteness from economic activity after the decline of <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD" title="Potosí">Potosí</a> and its silver industry and of the Liberal Party in the War of 1899. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bolivia" title="Constitution of Bolivia">2009 Constitution</a> assigns the role of national capital to Sucre, not referring to La Paz in the text.<sup id="cite_ref-presidencia.gob.bo_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-presidencia.gob.bo-125">[123]</a></sup> In addition to being the constitutional capital, the Supreme Court of Bolivia is located in Sucre, making it the judicial capital. Nonetheless, the <a href="/wiki/Palacio_Quemado" title="Palacio Quemado">Palacio Quemado</a> (the Presidential Palace and seat of Bolivian <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive power</a>) is located in La Paz, as are the National Congress and Plurinational Electoral Organ. La Paz thus continues to be the seat of government. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_crime">Law and crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Law and crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Bolivia" title="Crime in Bolivia">Crime in Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are 54 <a href="/wiki/Prisons_in_Bolivia" title="Prisons in Bolivia">prisons in Bolivia</a>, which incarcerate around 8,700 people as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. The prisons are managed by the Penitentiary Regime Directorate (Spanish: <i lang="es">Dirección de Régimen Penintenciario</i>). There are 17 prisons in <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Bolivia" title="Departments of Bolivia">departmental</a> capital cities and 36 provincial prisons.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Bolivia" title="Foreign relations of Bolivia">Foreign relations of Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:El_Salvador_President_at_Maduro_inauguration_2019_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/El_Salvador_President_at_Maduro_inauguration_2019_02.jpg/220px-El_Salvador_President_at_Maduro_inauguration_2019_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/El_Salvador_President_at_Maduro_inauguration_2019_02.jpg/330px-El_Salvador_President_at_Maduro_inauguration_2019_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/El_Salvador_President_at_Maduro_inauguration_2019_02.jpg/440px-El_Salvador_President_at_Maduro_inauguration_2019_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:El_Salvador_President_at_Maduro_inauguration_2019_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Presidents of Bolivia, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a> greet <a href="/wiki/Nicol%C3%A1s_Maduro" title="Nicolás Maduro">Nicolás Maduro</a> at Maduro's second inauguration in <a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">Caracas</a> on 10 January 2019
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Despite losing its maritime coast, the so-called <a href="/wiki/Litoral_Department" title="Litoral Department">Litoral Department</a>, after the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a>, Bolivia has historically maintained, as a state policy, a maritime claim to that part of <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>; the claim asks for sovereign access to the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a> and its maritime space. The issue has also been presented before the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>; in 1979, the OAS passed the <i>426 Resolution</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup> which declared that the Bolivian problem is a hemispheric problem. On 4 April 1884, a truce was signed with Chile, whereby Chile gave facilities of access to Bolivian products through <a href="/wiki/Antofagasta" title="Antofagasta">Antofagasta</a>, and freed the payment of export rights in the port of <a href="/wiki/Arica" title="Arica">Arica</a>. In October 1904, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Peace_and_Friendship_(1904)" title="Treaty of Peace and Friendship (1904)">Treaty of Peace and Friendship</a> was signed, and Chile agreed to build a <a href="/wiki/Arica%E2%80%93La_Paz_railway" title="Arica–La Paz railway">railway between Arica and La Paz</a>, to improve access of Bolivian products to the ports. </p>
      <p>The <i>Special Economical Zone for Bolivia in Ilo</i> (ZEEBI) is a special economic area of 5 kilometres (3.1 miles) of maritime coast, and a total extension of 358 <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">hectares</a> (880 acres), called Mar Bolivia ("Sea Bolivia"), where Bolivia may maintain a free port near <a href="/wiki/Ilo,_Peru" title="Ilo, Peru">Ilo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> under its administration and operation<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (July 2013)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup> for a period of 99 years starting in 1992; once that time has passed, all the construction and territory revert to the Peruvian government. Since 1964, Bolivia has had its own port facilities in the <i>Bolivian Free Port</i> in <a href="/wiki/Rosario,_Santa_Fe" title="Rosario, Santa Fe">Rosario, Argentina</a>. This port is located on the <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_River" title="Paraná River">Paraná River</a>, which is directly connected to the Atlantic Ocean. </p>
      <p>The dispute with Chile was taken to the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a>. The court ruled in support of the Chilean position, and declared that although Chile may have held talks about a Bolivian corridor to the sea, the country was not required to negotiate one or to surrender its territory.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Bolivia" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Bolivia">Bolivian military</a> comprises three branches: <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_Army" title="Bolivian Army">Ejército (Army)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_Naval_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolivian Naval Force">Naval (Navy)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_Air_Force" title="Bolivian Air Force">Fuerza Aérea (Air Force)</a>. The legal age for voluntary admissions is 18; however, when numbers are small the government in the past has recruited people as young as 14.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tour_of_duty" title="Tour of duty">tour of duty</a> is generally 12 months. </p>
      <p>The Bolivian army has around 31,500 men. There are six military regions (<i>regiones militares</i>—RMs) in the army. The army is organized into ten divisions. Although it is landlocked Bolivia keeps a navy. The <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_Naval_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolivian Naval Force">Bolivian Naval Force</a> (<i>Fuerza Naval Boliviana</i> in Spanish) is a naval force about 5,000 strong in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_Air_Force" title="Bolivian Air Force">Bolivian Air Force</a> ('Fuerza Aérea Boliviana' or 'FAB') has nine air bases, located at La Paz, Cochabamba, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_la_Sierra" title="Santa Cruz de la Sierra">Santa Cruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Su%C3%A1rez" title="Puerto Suárez">Puerto Suárez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tarija,_Bolivia" class="mw-redirect" title="Tarija, Bolivia">Tarija</a>, <a href="/wiki/Villamontes" title="Villamontes">Villamontes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cobija" title="Cobija">Cobija</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riberalta" title="Riberalta">Riberalta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robor%C3%A9" title="Roboré">Roboré</a>. </p>
      <p>In 2018, Bolivia signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Bolivian government annually spends $130&nbsp;million on defense.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Bolivia" title="Departments of Bolivia">Departments of Bolivia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Bolivia" title="Provinces of Bolivia">Provinces of Bolivia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Bolivia" title="Municipalities of Bolivia">Municipalities of Bolivia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Bolivia" title="Cantons of Bolivia">Cantons of Bolivia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Native_Community_Lands" title="Native Community Lands">Native Community Lands</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Bolivia has nine departments—<a href="/wiki/Pando_Department" title="Pando Department">Pando</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Paz_Department_(Bolivia)" title="La Paz Department (Bolivia)">La Paz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beni_Department" title="Beni Department">Beni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oruro_Department" title="Oruro Department">Oruro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba_Department" title="Cochabamba Department">Cochabamba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Department_(Bolivia)" title="Santa Cruz Department (Bolivia)">Santa Cruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD_Department" title="Potosí Department">Potosí</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chuquisaca_Department" title="Chuquisaca Department">Chuquisaca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tarija_Department" title="Tarija Department">Tarija</a>. </p>
      <p>According to what is established by the Bolivian Political Constitution, the Law of Autonomies and Decentralization regulates the procedure for the elaboration of Statutes of Autonomy, the transfer and distribution of direct competences between the central government and the autonomous entities.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are four levels of decentralization: Departmental government, constituted by the <i>Departmental Assembly</i>, with rights over the legislation of the department. The <a href="/wiki/Governor" title="Governor">governor</a> is chosen by <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a>. Municipal government, constituted by a <i>Municipal Council</i>, with rights over the legislation of the municipality. The <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a> is chosen by universal suffrage. Regional government, formed by several provinces or municipalities of geographical continuity within a department. It is constituted by a <i>Regional Assembly</i>. Original indigenous government, <a href="/wiki/Self-governance" title="Self-governance">self-governance</a> of original indigenous people on the ancient territories where they live. </p>
