      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Bolivia" title="Economy of Bolivia">Economy of Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg/250px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg" decoding="async" width="250" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg/375px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg/500px-Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1106" data-file-height="864"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Bolivia.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of Bolivia's product exports in 28 color-coded categories
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Avenida_Mariscal_Santa_Cruz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Avenida_Mariscal_Santa_Cruz.jpg/220px-Avenida_Mariscal_Santa_Cruz.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Avenida_Mariscal_Santa_Cruz.jpg/330px-Avenida_Mariscal_Santa_Cruz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Avenida_Mariscal_Santa_Cruz.jpg/440px-Avenida_Mariscal_Santa_Cruz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="853"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Avenida_Mariscal_Santa_Cruz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>La Paz, the financial center of Bolivia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bolivia's estimated 2012 gross domestic product (GDP) totaled $27.43 billion at official exchange rate and $56.14 billion at purchasing power parity. Despite a series of mostly political setbacks, between 2006 and 2009 the Morales administration has spurred growth higher than at any point in the preceding 30 years. The growth was accompanied by a moderate decrease in inequality.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> Under Morales per capita GDP doubled from US$1,182 in 2006 to US$2,238 in 2012. GDP growth under Morales averaged 5 percent a year, and in 2014 only <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> performed better in all of Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-138">[136]</a></sup> Bolivia's nominal GDP increased from 11.5 billion in 2006 to 41 billion in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bolivia in 2016 boasted the highest proportional rate of financial reserves of any nation in the world, with Bolivia's rainy day fund totaling some US$15 billion or nearly two-thirds of total annual GDP, up from a fifth of GDP in 2005. Even the IMF was impressed by Morales' fiscal prudence.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-138">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A major blow to the Bolivian economy came with a drastic fall in the price of tin during the early 1980s, which impacted one of Bolivia's main sources of income and one of its major mining industries.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup> Since 1985, the government of Bolivia has implemented a far-reaching program of macroeconomic stabilization and structural reform aimed at maintaining price stability, creating conditions for sustained growth, and alleviating scarcity. A major reform of the customs service has significantly improved transparency in this area. Parallel legislative reforms have locked into place market-liberal policies, especially in the hydrocarbon and telecommunication sectors, that have encouraged private investment. Foreign investors are accorded national treatment.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Miners_at_Work_Potosi_(pixinn.net).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/220px-Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/330px-Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg/440px-Miners_at_Work_Potosi_%28pixinn.net%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1702"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Miners_at_Work_Potosi_(pixinn.net).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Young miners at work in <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD" title="Potosí">Potosí</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In April 2000, Hugo Banzer, the former president of Bolivia, signed a contract with Aguas del Tunari, a private consortium, to operate and improve the water supply in Bolivia's third-largest city, <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba" title="Cochabamba">Cochabamba</a>. Shortly thereafter, the company tripled the water rates in that city, an action which resulted in <a href="/wiki/2000_Cochabamba_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2000 Cochabamba protests">protests and rioting</a> among those who could no longer afford clean water.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> Amidst Bolivia's nationwide economic collapse and growing national unrest over the state of the economy, the Bolivian government was forced to withdraw the water contract. </p>
      <p>Bolivia has the second largest <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> reserves in South America.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup> The government has a long-term sales agreement to sell natural gas to Brazil through 2019. The government held a binding referendum in 2005 on the Hydrocarbon Law. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">US Geological Service</a> estimates that Bolivia has 5.4 million <a href="/wiki/Cubic_ton" title="Cubic ton">cubic tonnes</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">lithium</a>, which represent 50%–70% of world reserves. However, to mine for it would involve disturbing the country's salt flats (called <a href="/wiki/Salar_de_Uyuni" title="Salar de Uyuni">Salar de Uyuni</a>), an important natural feature which boosts tourism in the region. The government does not want to destroy this unique natural landscape to meet the rising world demand for lithium.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> On the other hand, sustainable extraction of lithium is attempted by the government. This project is carried out by the public company "Recursos Evaporíticos" subsidiary of COMIBOL. </p>
      <p>It is thought that due to the importance of lithium for batteries for <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle" title="Electric vehicle">electric vehicles</a> and stabilization of electric grids with large proportions of intermittent <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewables</a> in the electricity mix, Bolivia could be strengthened geopolitically. However, this perspective has also been criticized for underestimating the power of economic incentives for expanded production in other parts of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-146">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Once Bolivia's government depended heavily on foreign assistance to finance development projects and to pay the public staff. At the end of 2002, the government owed $4.5 billion to its foreign <a href="/wiki/Creditor" title="Creditor">creditors</a>, with $1.6 billion of this amount owed to other governments and most of the balance owed to multilateral development banks. Most payments to other governments have been rescheduled on several occasions since 1987 through the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Club" title="Paris Club">Paris Club</a> mechanism. External creditors have been willing to do this because the Bolivian government has generally achieved the monetary and fiscal targets set by IMF programs since 1987, though economic crises have undercut Bolivia's normally good record. However, by 2013 the foreign assistance is just a fraction of the government budget thanks to tax collection mainly from the profitable exports to Brazil and Argentina of natural gas. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign-exchange_reserves">Foreign-exchange reserves</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Foreign-exchange reserves">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The amount in reserve currencies and <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> held by Bolivia's Central Bank advanced from 1.085 billion US dollars in 2000, under <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Banzer_Suarez" class="mw-redirect" title="Hugo Banzer Suarez">Hugo Banzer Suarez</a>'s government, to 15.282 billion US dollars in 2014 under <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a>' government. </p>

        </tr>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Bolivia" title="Tourism in Bolivia">Tourism in Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:908px">
       <div class="thumbinner">
        <div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Isla_del_Pescado,_Salar_de_Uyuni.jpg" class="image" title="Salar de Uyuni, one of the most visited sites in Bolivia."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Isla_del_Pescado%2C_Salar_de_Uyuni.jpg/900px-Isla_del_Pescado%2C_Salar_de_Uyuni.jpg" decoding="async" width="900" height="255" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Isla_del_Pescado%2C_Salar_de_Uyuni.jpg/1350px-Isla_del_Pescado%2C_Salar_de_Uyuni.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Isla_del_Pescado%2C_Salar_de_Uyuni.jpg/1800px-Isla_del_Pescado%2C_Salar_de_Uyuni.jpg 2x" data-file-width="11207" data-file-height="3178"></a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Isla_del_Pescado,_Salar_de_Uyuni.jpg" title="File:Isla del Pescado, Salar de Uyuni.jpg"> </a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Salar_de_Uyuni" title="Salar de Uyuni">Salar de Uyuni</a>, one of the most visited sites in Bolivia.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The income from tourism has become increasingly important. <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Bolivia" title="Tourism in Bolivia">Bolivia's tourist industry</a> has placed an emphasis on attracting ethnic diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-Xie2011_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xie2011-149">[147]</a></sup> The most visited places include <a href="/wiki/Nevado_Sajama" title="Nevado Sajama">Nevado Sajama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Torotoro_National_Park" title="Torotoro National Park">Torotoro National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madidi_National_Park" title="Madidi National Park">Madidi National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiwanaku" title="Tiwanaku">Tiwanaku</a> and the city of <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a>. </p>
      <p>The best known of the various festivals found in the country is the "<a href="/wiki/Carnaval_de_Oruro" title="Carnaval de Oruro">Carnaval de Oruro</a>", which was among the first 19 "<a href="/wiki/Masterpieces_of_the_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity" title="Masterpieces of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity">Masterpieces of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity</a>", as proclaimed by UNESCO in May 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-protection_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-protection-150">[148]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Bolivia's <a href="/wiki/Yungas_Road" title="Yungas Road">Yungas Road</a> was called the "world's most dangerous road" by the <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_Development_Bank" title="Inter-American Development Bank">Inter-American Development Bank</a>, called (<i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">El Camino de la Muerte</i>) in Spanish.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup> The northern portion of the road, much of it unpaved and without guardrails, was cut into the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Oriental_(Bolivia)" title="Cordillera Oriental (Bolivia)">Cordillera Oriental Mountain</a> in the 1930s. The fall from the narrow 12 feet (3.7&nbsp;m) path is as much as 2,000 feet (610&nbsp;m) in some places and due to the humid weather from the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon</a> there are often poor conditions like mudslides and falling rocks.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup> Each year over 25,000 bikers cycle along the 40 miles (64&nbsp;km) road. In 2018, an Israeli woman was killed by a falling rock while cycling on the road.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Apolo,_La_Paz" title="Apolo, La Paz">Apolo</a> road goes deep into <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a>. Roads in this area were originally built to allow access to <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mines</a> located near <a href="/wiki/Charazani" title="Charazani">Charazani</a>. Other noteworthy roads run to <a href="/wiki/Coroico" title="Coroico">Coroico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sorata" title="Sorata">Sorata</a>, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Zongo_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Zongo Valley (page does not exist)">Zongo Valley</a> (<a href="/wiki/Illimani" title="Illimani">Illimani</a> mountain), and along the <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba_Department" title="Cochabamba Department">Cochabamba</a> highway (<i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">carretera</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup> According to researchers with the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_International_Forestry_Research" title="Center for International Forestry Research">Center for International Forestry Research</a> (CIFOR), Bolivia's road network was still underdeveloped as of 2014. In lowland areas of Bolivia there is less than 2,000 kilometres (2,000,000&nbsp;m) of paved road. There have been some recent investments; <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">animal husbandry</a> has expanded in <a href="/wiki/Guayaramer%C3%ADn" title="Guayaramerín">Guayaramerín</a>, which might be due to a new road connecting Guayaramerín with <a href="/wiki/Trinidad,_Bolivia" title="Trinidad, Bolivia">Trinidad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_traffic">Air traffic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Air traffic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_airlines_of_Bolivia" title="List of airlines of Bolivia">List of airlines of Bolivia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Bolivia" title="List of airports in Bolivia">List of airports in Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg/220px-Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg/330px-Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg/440px-Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Aviones_de_BoA_en_Cochabamba.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Boliviana_de_Aviaci%C3%B3n" title="Boliviana de Aviación">Boliviana de Aviación</a> (BoA) is a state-owned company and the country's largest airline. Two BoA Boeing 737-300s parked at <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Wilstermann_International_Airport" title="Jorge Wilstermann International Airport">Jorge Wilstermann International Airport</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The General Directorate of Civil Aeronautics (Dirección General de Aeronáutica Civil—DGAC) formerly part of the FAB, administers a civil aeronautics school called the National Institute of Civil Aeronautics (Instituto Nacional de Aeronáutica Civil—INAC), and two commercial air transport services TAM and TAB. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/TAM_%E2%80%93_Transporte_A%C3%A9reo_Militar" title="TAM – Transporte Aéreo Militar">TAM – Transporte Aéreo Militar</a> (the Bolivian Military Airline) was an airline based in La Paz, Bolivia. It was the civilian wing of the 'Fuerza Aérea Boliviana' (the Bolivian Air Force), operating passenger services to remote towns and communities in the North and Northeast of Bolivia. TAM (a.k.a. TAM Group 71) has been a part of the FAB since 1945. The airline company has suspended its operations since 23 September 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Boliviana_de_Aviaci%C3%B3n" title="Boliviana de Aviación">Boliviana de Aviación</a>, often referred to as simply BoA, is the flag carrier airline of Bolivia and is wholly owned by the country's government.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A private airline serving regional destinations is <a href="/wiki/L%C3%ADnea_A%C3%A9rea_Amaszonas" title="Línea Aérea Amaszonas">Línea Aérea Amaszonas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup> with services including some international destinations. </p>
      <p>Although a civil transport airline, <a href="/wiki/TAB_%E2%80%93_Transportes_A%C3%A9reos_Bolivianos" class="mw-redirect" title="TAB – Transportes Aéreos Bolivianos">TAB – Transportes Aéreos Bolivianos</a>, was created as a subsidiary company of the FAB in 1977. It is subordinate to the Air Transport Management (Gerencia de Transportes Aéreos) and is headed by an FAB general. TAB, a charter heavy cargo airline, links Bolivia with most countries of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>; its inventory includes a fleet of Hercules C130 aircraft. TAB is headquartered adjacent to <a href="/wiki/El_Alto_International_Airport" title="El Alto International Airport">El Alto International Airport</a>. TAB flies to <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> and <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, with a stop in <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>. </p>
      <p>The three largest, and main international airports in Bolivia are <a href="/wiki/El_Alto_International_Airport" title="El Alto International Airport">El Alto International Airport</a> in La Paz, <a href="/wiki/Viru_Viru_International_Airport" title="Viru Viru International Airport">Viru Viru International Airport</a> in Santa Cruz, and <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Wilstermann_International_Airport" title="Jorge Wilstermann International Airport">Jorge Wilstermann International Airport</a> in Cochabamba. There are regional airports in other cities that connect to these three hubs.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railways">Railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Bolivia" title="Rail transport in Bolivia">Rail transport in Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Railways_in_Bolivia.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Railways_in_Bolivia.png/400px-Railways_in_Bolivia.png" decoding="async" width="400" height="251" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Railways_in_Bolivia.png/600px-Railways_in_Bolivia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Railways_in_Bolivia.png/800px-Railways_in_Bolivia.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="627"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Railways_in_Bolivia.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Railways in Bolivia <span class="nowrap">(<a href="//sharemap.org/public/Railways_in_Bolivia" class="extiw" title="sharemap:public/Railways in Bolivia">interactive map</a>)</span> 
         <br><span style="color:red">━━━</span> Routes with passenger traffic 
         <br><span style="color:black">━━━</span> Routes in usable state 
         <br><span style="color:black">··········</span> Unusable or dismantled routes
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bolivia possesses an extensive but aged rail system, all in 1000&nbsp;mm gauge, consisting of two disconnected networks. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Bolivia owns a <a href="/wiki/Communications_satellite" title="Communications satellite">communications satellite</a> which was <a href="/wiki/Offshore_company" title="Offshore company">offshored/outsourced</a> and launched by <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, named <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BApac_Katari_1" title="Túpac Katari 1">Túpac Katari 1</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup> In 2015, it was announced that electrical power advancements include a planned $300 million nuclear reactor developed by the <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> nuclear company <a href="/wiki/Rosatom" title="Rosatom">Rosatom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Water supply and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Bolivia" title="Water supply and sanitation in Bolivia">Water supply and sanitation in Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Bolivia's drinking water and <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a> coverage has greatly improved since 1990 due to a considerable increase in sectoral investment. However, the country has the continent's lowest coverage levels and services are of low quality. Political and institutional instability have contributed to the weakening of the sector's institutions at the national and local levels. </p>
      <p>Two concessions to foreign private companies in two of the three largest cities – <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba" title="Cochabamba">Cochabamba</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a>/<a href="/wiki/El_Alto" title="El Alto">El Alto</a> – were prematurely ended in 2000 and 2006 respectively. The country's second largest city, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_la_Sierra" title="Santa Cruz de la Sierra">Santa Cruz de la Sierra</a>, manages its own water and sanitation system relatively successfully by way of cooperatives. The government of <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a> intends to strengthen citizen participation within the sector. Increasing coverage requires a substantial increase of investment financing. </p>
      <p>According to the government the main problems in the sector are low access to sanitation throughout the country; low access to water in rural areas; insufficient and ineffective investments; a low visibility of community service providers; a lack of respect of indigenous customs; "technical and institutional difficulties in the design and implementation of projects"; a lack of capacity to operate and maintain infrastructure; an institutional framework that is "not consistent with the political change in the country"; "ambiguities in the social participation schemes"; a reduction in the quantity and quality of water due to climate change; pollution and a lack of integrated water resources management; and the lack of policies and programs for the reuse of wastewater.<sup id="cite_ref-PNSB_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PNSB-162">[160]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Only 27% of the population has access to <a href="/wiki/Improved_sanitation" title="Improved sanitation">improved sanitation</a>, 80 to 88% has access to <a href="/wiki/Improved_water_source" title="Improved water source">improved water sources</a>. Coverage in urban areas is bigger than in rural ones.<sup id="cite_ref-JMP_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JMP-163">[161]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Bolivia" title="Demographics of Bolivia">Demographics of Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-164">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-165">[163]</a></sup> </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Year </th> 
         <th style="background:#cfb;">Million </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">1950</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">3.1 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2000</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">8.3 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2018</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">11.4 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG/220px-Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG/330px-Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG/440px-Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Centro_de_La_Paz_en_Bolivia.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>People in La Paz city centre
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the last two censuses carried out by the Bolivian National Statistics Institute <i>(Instituto Nacional de Estadística</i>, INE), the population increased from 8,274,325 (from which 4,123,850 were men and 4,150,475 were women) in 2001 to 10,059,856 in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Cen2012_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cen2012-166">[164]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the last fifty years the Bolivian population has tripled, reaching a population growth rate of 2.25%. The growth of the population in the inter-census periods (1950–1976 and 1976–1992) was approximately 2.05%, while between the last period, 1992–2001, it reached 2.74% annually. </p>
      <p>Some 67.49% of Bolivians live in urban areas, while the remaining 32.51% in rural areas. The most part of the population (70%) is concentrated in the departments of <a href="/wiki/La_Paz_Department_(Bolivia)" title="La Paz Department (Bolivia)">La Paz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Department_(Bolivia)" title="Santa Cruz Department (Bolivia)">Santa Cruz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba_Department" title="Cochabamba Department">Cochabamba</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andean</a> <a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">Altiplano</a> region the departments of La Paz and <a href="/wiki/Oruro_Department" title="Oruro Department">Oruro</a> hold the largest percentage of population, in the valley region the largest percentage is held by the departments of Cochabamba and <a href="/wiki/Chuquisaca_Department" title="Chuquisaca Department">Chuquisaca</a>, while in the Llanos region by Santa Cruz and <a href="/wiki/Beni_Department" title="Beni Department">Beni</a>. At national level, the population density is 8.49, with variations marked between 0.8 (<a href="/wiki/Pando_Department" title="Pando Department">Pando Department</a>) and 26.2 (Cochabamba Department). </p>
      <p>The largest population center is located in the so-called "central axis" and in the Llanos region. Bolivia has a young population. According to the 2011 census, 59% of the population is between 15 and 59 years old, 39% is less than 15 years old. Almost 60% of the population is younger than 25 years of age. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Genetics">Genetics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Genetics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>According to a genetic study done on Bolivians, average values of Native American, European and African ancestry are 86%, 12.5%, and 1.5%, in individuals from La Paz and 76.8%, 21.4%, and 1.8% in individuals from Chuquisaca; respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_and_racial_classifications">Ethnic and racial classifications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Ethnic and racial classifications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_archer10_(Dennis)_-_Bolivia-133.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Aymara_people" title="Aymara people">Aymara</a> man, near Lake Titicaca, Bolivia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The vast majority of Bolivians are <a href="/wiki/Mestizo" title="Mestizo">mestizo</a> (with the indigenous component higher than the European one), although the government has not included the cultural self-identification "mestizo" in the November 2012 census.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup> There are approximately three dozen native groups totaling approximately half of the Bolivian population – the largest proportion of indigenous people in Latin America. Exact numbers vary based on the wording of the ethnicity question and the available response choices. For example, the 2001 census did not provide the racial category "mestizo" as a response choice, resulting in a much higher proportion of respondents identifying themselves as belonging to one of the available indigenous ethnicity choices. Mestizos are distributed throughout the entire country and make up 26% of the Bolivian population, with the predominantly mestizo departments being Beni, Santa Cruz, and Tarija. Most people assume their <i>mestizo</i> identity while at the same time identifying themselves with one or more indigenous cultures. A 2018 estimate of racial classification put mestizo (mixed white and Amerindian) at 68%, indigenous at 20%, white at 5%, <a href="/wiki/Cholo#Bolivia" title="Cholo">cholo</a> at 2%, black at 1%, other at 4%, while 2% were unspecified; 44% attributed themselves to some indigenous group, predominantly the linguistic categories of <a href="/wiki/Quechuas" class="mw-redirect" title="Quechuas">Quechuas</a> or <a href="/wiki/Aymara_people" title="Aymara people">Aymaras</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">whites</a> comprised about 14% of the population in 2006, and are usually concentrated in the largest cities: <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_la_Sierra" title="Santa Cruz de la Sierra">Santa Cruz de la Sierra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba" title="Cochabamba">Cochabamba</a>, but as well in some minor cities like <a href="/wiki/Tarija" title="Tarija">Tarija</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sucre" title="Sucre">Sucre</a>. The ancestry of whites and the white ancestry of mestizos lies within <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, most notably <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Department,_Bolivia" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Cruz Department, Bolivia">Santa Cruz Department</a>, there are several dozen colonies of German-speaking <a href="/wiki/Russian_Mennonite" title="Russian Mennonite">Mennonites from Russia</a> totaling around 40,000 inhabitants (as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Afro-Bolivian" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Bolivian">Afro-Bolivians</a>, descendants of <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">African slaves</a> who arrived in the time of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>, inhabit the <a href="/wiki/La_Paz_Department,_Bolivia" class="mw-redirect" title="La Paz Department, Bolivia">department of La Paz</a>, and are located mainly in the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Nor_Yungas_Province" title="Nor Yungas Province">Nor Yungas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sud_Yungas_Province" title="Sud Yungas Province">Sud Yungas</a>. Slavery was abolished in Bolivia in 1831.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup> There are also important communities of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Bolivians" title="Japanese Bolivians">Japanese</a> (14,000<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup>) and <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanese</a> (12,900<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup>). </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Indigenous peoples</a>, also called <i>"originarios"</i> ("native" or "original") and less frequently, <i>Amerindians</i>, could be categorized by geographic area, such as <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andean</a>, like the <a href="/wiki/Aymara_people" title="Aymara people">Aymaras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quechua_people" title="Quechua people">Quechuas</a> (who formed the ancient <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Inca Empire</a>), who are concentrated in the western departments of <a href="/wiki/La_Paz_Department,_Bolivia" class="mw-redirect" title="La Paz Department, Bolivia">La Paz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD_Department" title="Potosí Department">Potosí</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oruro_Department" title="Oruro Department">Oruro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba_Department" title="Cochabamba Department">Cochabamba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chuquisaca_Department" title="Chuquisaca Department">Chuquisaca</a>. There also are ethnic populations in the east, composed of the <a href="/wiki/Chiquitano" title="Chiquitano">Chiquitano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chan%C3%A9" title="Chané">Chané</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_people" title="Guaraní people">Guaraní</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moxo_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Moxo people">Moxos</a>, among others, who inhabit the departments of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Department,_Bolivia" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Cruz Department, Bolivia">Santa Cruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beni_Department" title="Beni Department">Beni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tarija_Department" title="Tarija Department">Tarija</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pando_Department" title="Pando Department">Pando</a>. </p>
      <p>There are small numbers of European citizens from <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, as well as from other countries of the Americas, as <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, among others. There are important <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peruvian</a> colonies in <a href="/wiki/La_Paz" title="La Paz">La Paz</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Alto" title="El Alto">El Alto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_la_Sierra" title="Santa Cruz de la Sierra">Santa Cruz de la Sierra</a>. </p>
      <p>There are around 140,000 <a href="/wiki/Mennonites_in_Bolivia" title="Mennonites in Bolivia">Mennonites in Bolivia</a> of Friesian, Flemish and German ethnic origins.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_peoples">Indigenous peoples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Indigenous peoples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Bolivia" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous peoples of Bolivia">Indigenous peoples of Bolivia</a> can be divided into two categories of ethnic groups: the Andeans, who are located in the <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andean</a> <a href="/wiki/Altiplano" title="Altiplano">Altiplano</a> and the valley region; and the lowland groups, who inhabit the warm regions of central and eastern Bolivia, including the valleys of Cochabamba Department, the Amazon Basin areas of northern La Paz Department, and the lowland departments of Beni, Pando, Santa Cruz, and Tarija (including the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Chaco" title="Gran Chaco">Gran Chaco</a> region in the southeast of the country). Large numbers of Andean peoples have also migrated to form Quechua, Aymara, and intercultural communities in the lowlands. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><b>Andean ethnicities</b> 
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/Aymara_people" title="Aymara people">Aymara people</a>. They live on the high plateau of the departments of La Paz, Oruro and Potosí, as well as some small regions near the tropical flatlands.</li> 
         <li><a href="/wiki/Quechua_people" title="Quechua people">Quechua people</a>. They mostly inhabit the valleys in <a href="/wiki/Cochabamba_Department" title="Cochabamba Department">Cochabamba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chuquisaca_Department" title="Chuquisaca Department">Chuquisaca</a>. They also inhabit some mountain regions in <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD_Department" title="Potosí Department">Potosí</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oruro_Department" title="Oruro Department">Oruro</a>. They divide themselves into different Quechua nations, as the Tarabucos, Ucumaris, Chalchas, Chaquies, Yralipes, Tirinas, among others.</li> 
         <li><a href="/wiki/Uru_people" title="Uru people">Uru people</a></li>
        </ul></li> 
       <li><b>Ethnicities of the Eastern Lowlands</b> 
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_people" title="Guaraní people">Guaraníes</a>: made up of Guarayos, Pausernas, <a href="/wiki/Sirion%C3%B3" title="Sirionó">Sirionós</a>, Chiriguanos, <a href="/wiki/Wich%C3%AD" title="Wichí">Wichí</a>, Chulipis, Taipetes, <a href="/wiki/Toba_people" title="Toba people">Tobas</a>, and Yuquis.</li> 
         <li><b>Tacanas</b>: made up of Lecos, Chimanes, Araonas, and Maropas.</li> 
         <li><b>Panos</b>: made up of Chacobos, Caripunas, Sinabos, Capuibos, and Guacanaguas.</li> 
         <li><b>Aruacos</b>: made up of Apolistas, Baures, <a href="/wiki/Moxo_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Moxo people">Moxos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chan%C3%A9_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Chané people">Chané</a>, Movimas, Cayabayas, Carabecas, and Paiconecas (Paucanacas).</li> 
         <li><b>Chapacuras</b>: made up of Itenez (More), Chapacuras, Sansinonianos, Canichanas, Itonamas, Yuracares, Guatoses, and <a href="/wiki/Chiquitano" title="Chiquitano">Chiquitanos</a>.</li> 
         <li><b>Botocudos</b>: made up of Bororos and Otuquis.</li> 
         <li><b>Zamucos</b>: made up of <a href="/wiki/Ayoreo_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ayoreo people">Ayoreos</a>.</li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="***REMOVED***">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Bolivia" title="Languages of Bolivia">Languages of Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png/220px-Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png/330px-Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png/440px-Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png 2x" data-file-width="2370" data-file-height="2672"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pueblos_originarios_de_Bolivia.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Geographic distribution of the indigenous languages of Bolivia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bolivia has great linguistic diversity as a result of its <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">multiculturalism</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bolivia" title="Constitution of Bolivia">Constitution of Bolivia</a> recognizes 36 official languages besides <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Araona_language" title="Araona language">Araona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baure_language" title="Baure language">Baure</a>, <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9siro_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Bésiro language">Bésiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canichana_language" title="Canichana language">Canichana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cavine%C3%B1o_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Cavineño language">Cavineño</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cayubaba_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Cayubaba language">Cayubaba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A1cobo_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Chácobo language">Chácobo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chim%C3%A1n_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Chimán language">Chimán</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ese_Ejja_language" title="Ese Ejja language">Ese Ejja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Guaraní language">Guaraní</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guarasuawe_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Guarasuawe language">Guarasu'we</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guarayu_language" title="Guarayu language">Guarayu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Itonama_language" title="Itonama language">Itonama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leco_language" title="Leco language">Leco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machajuyai-Kallawaya" class="mw-redirect" title="Machajuyai-Kallawaya">Machajuyai-Kallawaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machineri_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Machineri language">Machineri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maropa_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Maropa language">Maropa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moje%C3%B1o-Ignaciano" class="mw-redirect" title="Mojeño-Ignaciano">Mojeño-Ignaciano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moje%C3%B1o-Trinitario" class="mw-redirect" title="Mojeño-Trinitario">Mojeño-Trinitario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mor%C3%A9_language_(Bolivia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Moré language (Bolivia)">Moré</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moset%C3%A9n_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Mosetén language">Mosetén</a>, <a href="/wiki/Movima_language" title="Movima language">Movima</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pacawara_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacawara language">Pacawara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puquina_language" title="Puquina language">Puquina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quechua_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Quechua language">Quechua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sirion%C3%B3_language" title="Sirionó language">Sirionó</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tacana_language" title="Tacana language">Tacana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tapiet%C3%A9_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Tapieté language">Tapieté</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toromona_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Toromona language">Toromona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uru-Chipaya" class="mw-redirect" title="Uru-Chipaya">Uru-Chipaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weenhayek_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Weenhayek language">Weenhayek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yaminawa_language" title="Yaminawa language">Yaminawa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yuki_language_(Bolivia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Yuki language (Bolivia)">Yuki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yuracar%C3%A9_language" title="Yuracaré language">Yuracaré</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zamuco_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Zamuco language">Zamuco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-languages_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-languages-2">[2]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> is the most spoken official language in the country, according to the 2001 census; as it is spoken by two-thirds of the population. All legal and official documents issued by the State, including the Constitution, the main private and public institutions, the media, and commercial activities, are in Spanish. </p>
      <p>The main indigenous languages are: <a href="/wiki/Quechua_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Quechua language">Quechua</a> (21.2% of the population in the 2001 census), <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a> (14.6%), <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">Guarani</a> (0.6%) and others (0.4%) including the <a href="/wiki/Moxos_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Moxos language">Moxos</a> in the department of Beni.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Plautdietsch" class="mw-redirect" title="Plautdietsch">Plautdietsch</a>, a <a href="/wiki/German_dialects" title="German dialects">German dialect</a>, is spoken by about 70,000 <a href="/wiki/Mennonites_in_Bolivia" title="Mennonites in Bolivia">Mennonites</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Department_(Bolivia)" title="Santa Cruz Department (Bolivia)">Santa Cruz</a>. <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> is spoken mainly in the areas close to <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>. </p>
      <p>Bilingual education was implemented in Bolivia under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">President Evo Morales</a>. His program placed emphasis on the expansion of indigenous languages in the educational systems of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Bolivia" title="Religion in Bolivia">Religion in Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px"> 
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">

        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption"> 
         <p>Religion in Bolivia (2014)<sup id="cite_ref-Religion_in_Latin_America_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Religion_in_Latin_America-176">[174]</a></sup> </p> 
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Gold; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> (77%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Violet; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> (16%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:Chartreuse; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Other (3%)
         </div>
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:White; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Irreligious" class="mw-redirect" title="Irreligious">Irreligious</a> (4%)
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bolivia is a constitutionally <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a> that guarantees the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a> and the independence of government from religion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConstitute_Assembly_of_Bolivia20072_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConstitute_Assembly_of_Bolivia20072-177">[175]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the 2001 <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a> conducted by the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Bolivia" title="National Institute of Statistics of Bolivia">National Institute of Statistics of Bolivia</a>, 78% of the population is <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism">Roman Catholic</a>, followed by 19% that are <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>, as well as a small number of Bolivians that are <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox</a>, and 3% non-religious.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Religion_Data_Archives" title="Association of Religion Data Archives">Association of Religion Data Archives</a> (relying on the World Christian Database) records that in 2010, 92.5% of Bolivians identified as <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> (of any denomination), 3.1% identified with indigenous religion, 2.2% identified as <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí</a>, 1.9% identified as <a href="/wiki/Agnosticism" title="Agnosticism">agnostic</a>, and all other groups constituted 0.1% or less.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Much of the indigenous population adheres to different traditional beliefs marked by <a href="/wiki/Inculturation" title="Inculturation">inculturation</a> or <a href="/wiki/Syncretic" class="mw-redirect" title="Syncretic">syncretism</a> with Christianity. The cult of <a href="/wiki/Pachamama" title="Pachamama">Pachamama</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup> or "Mother Earth", is notable. The veneration of the <a href="/wiki/Virgen_de_Copacabana" title="Virgen de Copacabana">Virgin of Copacabana</a>, Virgin of Urkupiña and Virgin of Socavón, is also an important feature of <a href="/wiki/Christian_pilgrimage" title="Christian pilgrimage">Christian pilgrimage</a>. There also are important <a href="/wiki/Aymara_people" title="Aymara people">Aymaran communities</a> near <a href="/wiki/Lake_Titicaca" title="Lake Titicaca">Lake Titicaca</a> that have a strong devotion to <a href="/wiki/James,_son_of_Zebedee" class="mw-redirect" title="James, son of Zebedee">James the Apostle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup> Deities worshiped in Bolivia include <a href="/wiki/Ekeko" title="Ekeko">Ekeko</a>, the Aymaran god of abundance and prosperity, whose day is celebrated every 24 January, and <a href="/wiki/Guarani_mythology" title="Guarani mythology">Tupá</a>, a god of the <a href="/wiki/Guaran%C3%AD_people" title="Guaraní people">Guaraní people</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities_and_towns">Largest cities and towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Largest cities and towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Approximately 67% of Bolivians live in urban areas,<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-183">[181]</a></sup> among the lowest proportion in South America. Nevertheless, the rate of urbanization is growing steadily, at around 2.5% annually. According to the 2012 census, there are total of 3,158,691 households in Bolivia – an increase of 887,960 from 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-Cen2012_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cen2012-166">[164]</a></sup> In 2009, 75.4% of homes were classified as a house, hut, or Pahuichi; 3.3% were apartments; 21.1% were rental residences; and 0.1% were <a href="/wiki/Mobile_home" title="Mobile home">mobile homes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup> Most of the country's largest cities are located in the highlands of the west and central regions. </p>
      <p><br> </p> 
      <table style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; width: 100%; border: 1px solid darkgray; background: #f9f9f9">

      <p><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup> </p>
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Bolivia" title="Culture of Bolivia">Culture of Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Bolivia" title="Music of Bolivia">Music of Bolivia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Bolivia" title="Public holidays in Bolivia">Public holidays in Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg/220px-Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg/330px-Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg/440px-Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg 2x" data-file-width="652" data-file-height="489"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ni%C3%B1os_ejecutando_una_tarkeada.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bolivian children playing <a href="/wiki/Tarka_(flute)" title="Tarka (flute)">tarka</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bolivian culture has been heavily influenced by the Aymara, the Quechua, as well as the popular cultures of Latin America as a whole. </p>
      <p>The cultural development is divided into three distinct periods: precolumbian, colonial, and republican. Important <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">archaeological</a> ruins, gold and silver ornaments, stone monuments, <a href="/wiki/Ceramic" title="Ceramic">ceramics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Weaving" title="Weaving">weavings</a> remain from several important pre-Columbian cultures. Major ruins include <a href="/wiki/Tiwanaku" title="Tiwanaku">Tiwanaku</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Fuerte_de_Samaipata" title="El Fuerte de Samaipata">El Fuerte de Samaipata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inkallaqta" title="Inkallaqta">Inkallaqta</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Iskanawaya&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Iskanawaya (page does not exist)">Iskanawaya</a>. The country abounds in other sites that are difficult to reach and have seen little archaeological exploration.<sup id="cite_ref-BackgroundNote_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BackgroundNote-186">[184]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Diablada_oruro_fraternidad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Diablada_oruro_fraternidad.jpg/220px-Diablada_oruro_fraternidad.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Diablada_oruro_fraternidad.jpg/330px-Diablada_oruro_fraternidad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/ba/Diablada_oruro_fraternidad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="244"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Diablada_oruro_fraternidad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Diablada_of_Oruro" class="mw-redirect" title="Diablada of Oruro">Diablada</a>, dance primeval, typical and main of <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Oruro" class="mw-redirect" title="Carnival of Oruro">Carnival of Oruro</a> a <a href="/wiki/Masterpieces_of_the_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity" title="Masterpieces of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity">Masterpiece of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity</a> since 2001 in Bolivia (<i>File: Fraternidad Artística y Cultural "La Diablada"</i>)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Spanish brought their own tradition of religious art which, in the hands of local native and mestizo builders and <a href="/wiki/Artisan" title="Artisan">artisans</a>, developed into a rich and distinctive style of architecture, painting, and sculpture known as "Mestizo Baroque". The colonial period produced not only the paintings of Pérez de Holguín, Flores, Bitti, and others but also the works of skilled but unknown stonecutters, woodcarvers, goldsmiths, and silversmiths. An important body of Native Baroque religious music of the colonial period was recovered and has been performed internationally to wide acclaim since 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-BackgroundNote_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BackgroundNote-186">[184]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bolivian artists of stature in the 20th century include <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Luisa_Pacheco" title="María Luisa Pacheco">María Luisa Pacheco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Mamani_Mamani" title="Roberto Mamani Mamani">Roberto Mamani Mamani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Mario_Yllanes" title="Alejandro Mario Yllanes">Alejandro Mario Yllanes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Da_Silva" title="Alfredo Da Silva">Alfredo Da Silva</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marina_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez_del_Prado" title="Marina Núñez del Prado">Marina Núñez del Prado</a>. </p>
      <p>Bolivia has a rich <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folklore</a>. Its regional <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a> is distinctive and varied. The "devil dances" at the annual carnival of Oruro are one of the great folkloric events of South America, as is the lesser known carnival at <a href="/wiki/Tarabuco" title="Tarabuco">Tarabuco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BackgroundNote_186-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BackgroundNote-186">[184]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Bolivia" title="Education in Bolivia">Education in Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2008, following <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> standards, Bolivia was declared free of <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">illiteracy</a>, making it the fourth country in South America to attain this status.<sup id="cite_ref-literacyBBC_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-literacyBBC-187">[185]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bolivia has public and private universities. Among them: <a href="/wiki/University_of_Saint_Francis_Xavier" title="University of Saint Francis Xavier">Universidad Mayor, Real y Pontificia de San Francisco Xavier de Chuquisaca</a> USFX – Sucre, founded in 1624; <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Mayor_de_San_Andr%C3%A9s" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad Mayor de San Andrés">Universidad Mayor de San Andrés</a> UMSA – La Paz, founded in 1830; <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Mayor_de_San_Simon" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad Mayor de San Simon">Universidad Mayor de San Simon</a> UMSS – Cochabamba, founded in 1832; <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Aut%C3%B3noma_Gabriel_Ren%C3%A9_Moreno" title="Universidad Autónoma Gabriel René Moreno">Universidad Autónoma Gabriel René Moreno</a> UAGRM – Santa Cruz de la Sierra, founded in 1880; <a href="/wiki/Universidad_T%C3%A9cnica_de_Oruro" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad Técnica de Oruro">Universidad Técnica de Oruro</a> UTO – Oruro, founded in 1892; and <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Aut%C3%B3noma_Tom%C3%A1s_Fr%C3%ADas" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad Autónoma Tomás Frías">Universidad Autónoma Tomás Frías</a> UATF – Potosi, founded in 1892. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Bolivia" title="Health in Bolivia">Health in Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Refresh_Bolivia" title="Refresh Bolivia">Refresh Bolivia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>According to UNICEF under-five mortality rate in 2006 was 52.7 per 1000 and was reduced to 26 per 1000 by 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup> The infant mortality rate was 40.7 per 1000 in 2006 and was reduced to 21.2 per 1000 in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup> Before Morales took office, nearly half of all infants were not vaccinated; now nearly all are vaccinated. Morales also put into place several supplemental nutrition programs, including an effort to supply free food in public health and social security offices, and his desnutrición cero (zero malnutrition) program provides free school lunches.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_138-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-138">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Between 2006 and 2016, extreme poverty in Bolivia fell from 38.2% to 16.8%. Chronic malnutrition in children under five years of age also went down by 14% and the child mortality rate was reduced by more than 50%, according to <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup> In 2019 the Bolivian government created a universal healthcare system which has been cited as a model for all by the World Health Organization.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[189]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is popular. The national team is the <a href="/wiki/Bolivia_national_football_team" title="Bolivia national football team">Bolivia national football team</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Racquetball" title="Racquetball">Racquetball</a> is the second most popular sport in Bolivia as for the results in the Odesur 2018 Games held in Cochabamba.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bolivia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
